  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2d96c9e5-648b-45e2-923d-11c9191c043f'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer1878951163189851252">They're back: Calvin, the six-year-old dirty tricksmeister and master of indignation and his warm, cuddly philosopher sidekick, Hobbes. A tiger whose idea of adventure is to lie on his back by the fire and have his stomach rubbed. In six short years this unlikely duo has captured the hearts, the minds, and, most of all, the funny bones of America. They are the most phenome</span>
  <span id="freeText1878951163189851252" style="display:none">They're back: Calvin, the six-year-old dirty tricksmeister and master of indignation and his warm, cuddly philosopher sidekick, Hobbes. A tiger whose idea of adventure is to lie on his back by the fire and have his stomach rubbed. In six short years this unlikely duo has captured the hearts, the minds, and, most of all, the funny bones of America. They are the most phenomenal success story in syndication - and publishing - history. In only six years, they appear in more than 2,100 newspapers worldwide, and Calvin and Hobbes wins as many readership polls as Calvin has excesses. All seven of Bill Watterson's collections have sold a million copies within a year of publication. This treasury collection contains a never-before-published full-color section, as well as the cartoons appearing in 'The Revenge of the Baby-Sat' and 'Scientific Progress Goes "Boink."' All Sunday cartoons are presented full-page and full-color.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18243620260499741510">UPDATED! What can I possibly say? I love C&H. My kids love C&H. My daughter wants me to find her a Hobbes doll and REFUSES to accept Tigger as a substitute! Spaceman Spiff! Stupendous Man! Susie Derkins! Mom and Dad! Rosalyn! Miss Wormwood! A true classic and tickles your funny bones cover to cover!<br/><br/>Based on the comments below. I felt I needed to define the Holy Trinity of Intelligent Comics for Old Nincompoops (ICON) which for me would consist of Bill Watterson, the father and son, Berke Breathe</span>
  <span id="freeText18243620260499741510" style="display:none">UPDATED! What can I possibly say? I love C&amp;H. My kids love C&amp;H. My daughter wants me to find her a Hobbes doll and REFUSES to accept Tigger as a substitute! Spaceman Spiff! Stupendous Man! Susie Derkins! Mom and Dad! Rosalyn! Miss Wormwood! A true classic and tickles your funny bones cover to cover!<br /><br />Based on the comments below. I felt I needed to define the Holy Trinity of Intelligent Comics for Old Nincompoops (ICON) which for me would consist of Bill Watterson, the father and son, Berke Breathed -ACK!!, and Gary Larson the spirit of the absurd. Perhaps readers like me that grew up in the 70s and 80s to have a trait seemingly lost in the generations X++, perhaps some of you learned as much about critical thinking from C&amp;H, The Far Side and Bloom County than you did in your University classes on Philosophy and 20th C American Literature.</span>

  <span id="freeText10319322600975409307" style="display:none">I have an uncle who I’ll call Uncle Bob. Uncle Bob is an extremely tall man; he has a booming voice and commanding presence. When he’s in the room, it’s hard not to pay attention to Uncle Bob. And that’s good for him, because he likes the attention; he laughs and jokes constantly, and loves a good audience. In short, he’s a natural born salesman. So Uncle Bob naturally excelled when he got his first job out of college selling tractors. In fact, he was so good that now he trains everyone else. His company is very fond of him, so he has plenty of vacation, which he uses to fish, to play card games, and to snowmobile. He is not a man of literature.<br />		<br />So I was naturally intrigued to find him, one day, curled up over a book, snickering loudly. What book could it be? None other than this one. Curious, I started leafing through it when he left it on the table. I loved it. I showed it to my brother, and he loved it too. What a great comic! Maybe Uncle Bob’s a man of literature after all.</span>

<div id="review_257310487" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/257310487" />
    <a title="Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1492392-rose"><img alt="Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532185276p2/1492392.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/257310487?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/1492392-rose">Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780836218985" href="/book/show/297839.The_Indispensable_Calvin_and_Hobbes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1492392-rose?shelf=laughs">laughs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer257310487" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16407663616434648878">Trying to choose a favorite Calvin and Hobbes book really is not entirely unlike trying to choose a favorite child. These books were a seminal part of my childhood; I've reread them so many times throughout childhood, the teen years, and adulthood that I'm not exaggerating when I say that if you start quoting one of the strips, I can almost guarantee that I'll be able to give you the punchline from memory.<br/><br/>"The Indispensable Calvin and Hobbes" is a treasury made up of what may be my two favorite </span>
  <span id="freeText16407663616434648878" style="display:none">Trying to choose a favorite Calvin and Hobbes book really is not entirely unlike trying to choose a favorite child. These books were a seminal part of my childhood; I've reread them so many times throughout childhood, the teen years, and adulthood that I'm not exaggerating when I say that if you start quoting one of the strips, I can almost guarantee that I'll be able to give you the punchline from memory.<br /><br />"The Indispensable Calvin and Hobbes" is a treasury made up of what may be my two favorite Calvin and Hobbes books: "Revenge of the Baby-Sat" and "Scientific Progress Goes 'Boink'." I think the bulk of all my all-time favorite C&amp;H storylines are in here, including Calvin forgetting his bug report until the last minute (literally, the last minute), the Garage-as-Clubhouse incident (probably when I laughed the hardest at the strip), their first time-traveling adventure ("You mean we went into the past because we were FACING THE WRONG WAY??"), the army of Calvin clones, Calvin signing up to play baseball at recess (all my inner childhood angst about organized sports seemed to have been poured upon the page for this storyline) ... and my absolute all-time favorite, which I still relate to so strongly today: Calvin's mail-order beanie.<br /><br />If I could only have one Calvin and Hobbes book, it would be this collection. Thankfully, I'm pleased to say I've got them all! (Although, I really need to start buying new copies. A lot of them are falling apart from being reread so often ...)</span>
  <a data-text-id="16407663616434648878" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=childrens-literature">childrens-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=childhood-favourites">childhood-favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer707519278" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2722128783969367797">The best thing about the Calvin and Hobbes books is that I grew up just looking at the pictures because I didn't read English, but found them so funny nevertheless. Then, when I learned English and was finally able to read them, they were even funnier because I could finally understand what the characters were saying. And as I grow a bit older and wiser, I still laugh whenever I crack one open, but for entirely different reasons. I love how there is something for every age in these books. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_195894504" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/195894504" />
    <a title="Alice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1247026-alice"><img alt="Alice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285199742p2/1247026.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/195894504?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alice" href="/user/show/1247026-alice">Alice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780836218985" href="/book/show/297839.The_Indispensable_Calvin_and_Hobbes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1247026-alice?shelf=wishlist">wishlist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1247026-alice?shelf=many-happy-rereads">many-happy-rereads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1247026-alice?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1247026-alice?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1247026-alice?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1247026-alice?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer195894504" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13093261021957071799">I just happened to pick this book up while visiting a friend, and, the next thing I knew, it was hours later. I read these when they were originally syndicated in my hometown newspaper, and I read <i>Scientific Progress Goes "Boink"</i> and <i>The Revenge of the Baby-Sat</i>. I could read these a million times and still want to read them again.<br/><br/>These are definitely written to be appreciated on several levels, which is what makes them so rereadable. I had one perspective on them when I was young, and another no</span>
  <span id="freeText13093261021957071799" style="display:none">I just happened to pick this book up while visiting a friend, and, the next thing I knew, it was hours later. I read these when they were originally syndicated in my hometown newspaper, and I read <i>Scientific Progress Goes "Boink"</i> and <i>The Revenge of the Baby-Sat</i>. I could read these a million times and still want to read them again.<br /><br />These are definitely written to be appreciated on several levels, which is what makes them so rereadable. I had one perspective on them when I was young, and another now that I'm all grown up, myself. Calvin's antics aren't laugh-out-loud funny anymore, but bittersweet now that I can imagine raising such a holy terror. And the section about the break-in at their home, instead of inspiring boredom, seems very apt, and I can sympathize with the parents. I finally see the humor in Calvin's declaration that this is the coolest thing to happen to him.<br /><br />Most interesting is that I never understood how a bright kid like Calvin could do so poorly in school. It makes sense now, and I even understand why I didn't see it, before. Calvin's school isn't about nurturing creativity or teaching children to use their gifts. It's about teaching kids to sit down, shut up, and do their homework. Calvin is at his worst when he's told to obey for reasons that make no sense to him, and so of course he's going to the principal's office daily.<br /><br />Watterson also manages to paint a decent view of the female perspective, despite Calvin's view of girls as gross and slimy, and his mother as a dispenser of disgusting food, clean laundry, and torturous baths. I got the feeling that he really gets it.<br /><br />I need to remember to brighten my view with one of these books from time to time. We all need a little more imagination in our lives.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13093261021957071799" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3141031814" />
    <a title="Jaimie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8659422-jaimie"><img alt="Jaimie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1334447810p2/8659422.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3141031814?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jaimie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jaimie" href="/user/show/8659422-jaimie">Jaimie</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3141031814" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12057359723170647530">Now here's the Calvin and Hobbes collection to read during the Winter months! Calvin spends so much of his time wishing for winter to come, and it's finally here - complete with monstrous snowmen, snowball fights, and plenty of sledding mishaps! While Calvin revels in the glory of a 12 inch snowfall and warming up in front of the fire, the overall tone of the volume was a bit darker than some of the other collections. Not only does Calvin himself have a few moments where he laments the fate of t</span>
  <span id="freeText12057359723170647530" style="display:none">Now here's the Calvin and Hobbes collection to read during the Winter months! Calvin spends so much of his time wishing for winter to come, and it's finally here - complete with monstrous snowmen, snowball fights, and plenty of sledding mishaps! While Calvin revels in the glory of a 12 inch snowfall and warming up in front of the fire, the overall tone of the volume was a bit darker than some of the other collections. Not only does Calvin himself have a few moments where he laments the fate of the bullied, wasting his childhood with homework, and the struggles of team sports, we are also treated to a few comics which are told from the perspective of his father. Unlike Calvin, his father is a realist, and this makes his outlook a lot more dour even if he does take a few moments to distance himself from his adult life to play with Calvin. In terms of the chronology of Calvin's life, this collection is comprised of his later years, so maybe this is the turning point where we see Calvin starting to grow up and out of his childhood innocence. He has to grow up eventually, doesn't he? Or maybe not, since Calvin and Hobbes are kind of in the same league as Peter Pan and seem to stay childlike forever. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12057359723170647530" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_258998093" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Paul Darcy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7368831-paul-darcy"><img alt="Paul Darcy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1326027182p2/7368831.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/258998093?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul Darcy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul Darcy" href="/user/show/7368831-paul-darcy">Paul Darcy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7368831-paul-darcy?shelf=comics">comics</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer258998093" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9687082012475935475">by Bill Watterson, published in 1992.<br/><br/>Another fantastic collection of Watterson’s Calvin and Hobbes cartoons. There is just so much fun and mayhem to enjoy in this collection it’s hard to quantify how great it is.<br/><br/>This collection, “The Indispensable Calvin and Hobbes”, is the collected cartoons of “The Revenge of the Baby-Sat” and “Scientific Progress goes “Boink”. Absolutely fantastic fun.<br/><br/>In this collection we get to see the first appearance of Stupendous Man, Defender of Freedom, Advocate of Lib</span>
  <span id="freeText9687082012475935475" style="display:none">by Bill Watterson, published in 1992.<br /><br />Another fantastic collection of Watterson’s Calvin and Hobbes cartoons. There is just so much fun and mayhem to enjoy in this collection it’s hard to quantify how great it is.<br /><br />This collection, “The Indispensable Calvin and Hobbes”, is the collected cartoons of “The Revenge of the Baby-Sat” and “Scientific Progress goes “Boink”. Absolutely fantastic fun.<br /><br />In this collection we get to see the first appearance of Stupendous Man, Defender of Freedom, Advocate of Liberty! And yes, hilarity ensues every time Calvin puts on the caped costume and assumes the role.<br /><br />Also we get to see the formation of G.R.O.S.S, or Get Rid Of Slimy girlS. We get to see just how much Calvin does not enjoy camping with his parents, how he gets attacked by his food, how he is trapped in a world where, for him, gravity reverses itself and on and on.<br /><br />Other fantastic pleasures arise when we meet “Tracer Bullet”, private eye. And my personal favourite had to be the “Duplicator”, which is Calvin’s old Transmogrifier cardboard box renamed.<br /><br />He makes a duplicate of himself, and then the duplicate makes more duplicates until the house is filling up with Calvins. And yes, each one is just as naughty as the original. Great fun, and a great solution in the end of how the real Calvin deals with them - but I won’t give it away and spoil the fun.<br /><br />And all your favourites are here as well. This means more adventures of Spaceman Spiff, toboggan rides, wagon rides and Calvin as many types of dinosaur.<br /><br />Oh, and one more thing I will mention. We begin to see snowmen. But not regular snowmen, but the house of horror snowmen, or the city of snowmen that dinosaur Calvin stomps and eats. Very funny stuff which come to a climax in future installments of the cartoons.<br /><br />Not to be missed, this treasury is a goldmine of humour and what it is to be, and live with, a mischievous six year old boy and his tiger.<br /><br />For those wishing to collect all the strips of Calvin and Hobbes I provide the complete paperback listing below. <br /><br />The complete Calvin and Hobbes trade paperback list: (all the Calvin and Hobbes strips, but you don’t need to collect all the paperback editions that are out there to get them.)<br /><br />This list will give you all the strips without having to collect all the paperback editions out there.<br /><br />1) The Essential Calvin and Hobbes<br />2) The Indispensable Calvin and Hobbes<br />3) The Authoritative Calvin and Hobbes<br />4) Attack of the Deranged Mutant Killer Monster Snow Goons<br />5) The Days are Just Packed<br />6) Homicidal Psycho Jungle Cat<br />7) There’s Treasure Everywhere<br />8) It’s a Magical World<br /><br />9) The Calvin and Hobbes Tenth Anniversary Book (Optional, this volume has lots of duplicates from the other collections and only a few strips that don’t appear anywhere else)</span>
  <a data-text-id="9687082012475935475" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7154785342184195491">A Thousand, Million Goodreads stars.<br/><br/>I couple of years ago, I reread all of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/210000181?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Far Side Gallaries</a>. (Or so I had thought... Apparently, I missed Gallery 5...)<br/><br/>But when it comes to my life, no comic/cartoon/Sunday Funny has been read by me more than Calvin and Hobbes. Indeed, Watterson may be the most influential writer in my life. I have more "goodreads quotes" in my goodreads quote section than any other author. And it's not even close.<br/><br/>I want to retell the story of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/381309371?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>being banned from reading</a>, or t</span>
  <span id="freeText7154785342184195491" style="display:none">A Thousand, Million Goodreads stars.<br><br>I couple of years ago, I reread all of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/210000181?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">The Far Side Gallaries</a>. (Or so I had thought... Apparently, I missed Gallery 5...)<br><br>But when it comes to my life, no comic/cartoon/Sunday Funny has been read by me more than Calvin and Hobbes. Indeed, Watterson may be the most influential writer in my life. I have more "goodreads quotes" in my goodreads quote section than any other author. And it's not even close.<br><br>I want to retell the story of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/381309371?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">being banned from reading</a>, or tell about the game my college roommate and I played where we'd flip open to any random page in any Calvin and Hobbes book and start a quote, and the other would have to finish it.<br><br>Calvin improved my vocabulary, taught me subtlety (from his lack), and how sometimes friends are jerks. And often you're the jerk, but you can't recognize it in yourself.<br><br>At this moment in my life, though, when I read it I came away with something else. I finished this at the end of June, 2016. Here in the U.S. we're in the middle of a... ...an interesting presidential cycle.<br><br>I noticed that Calvin <i>is</i> Donald Trump.<br><br>Now, who knows? Maybe Trump will turn out to be a fine president. But Calvin seems to often match up with the persona Trump is creating. I was so taken by this revelation that I took a bunch of screen shots and <a href="https://www.facebook.com/philip.habecker/posts/10154337160638934?pnref=story" rel="nofollow noopener">posted it to Facebook</a>. As it turns out, I wasn't the only one who noticed.<br><br>As I said in my post, I feel bad about tying one of my childhood heroes to a person I personally don't care for. (True, on Facebook I was a little more direct in my feelings toward Mr. Trump...) But, lots of people took notice and have been photoshopping Trump's face over Calvin's face. I'm still not sure how to take it.<br><br><a href="https://www.reddit.com/r/DonaldandHobbes/" rel="nofollow noopener">Check it out.</a><br><br>Here's a preview:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467428480i/19591534._SX540_.png" alt="Inheritance" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467428480i/19591535._SX540_.jpg" alt="The News" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467428292i/19591531._SY540_.png" alt="Made Up Fact" class="gr-hostedUserImg">.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2970058152" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16510336409616183505">I can’t seem to get enough of Calvin and Hobbes these days and have been slowly making my way through all available collections at the library. I’m coming to really appreciate the different personalities of the secondary characters – the dad, the mom, Susie Derkins, Moe and Rosalyn. A lot of the content is also surprisingly still quite relatable in adulthood. How many times are we forced to do something we don’t want to do? How many times do we imagine we’re somewhere or someone else? Every morn</span>
  <span id="freeText16510336409616183505" style="display:none">I can’t seem to get enough of Calvin and Hobbes these days and have been slowly making my way through all available collections at the library. I’m coming to really appreciate the different personalities of the secondary characters – the dad, the mom, Susie Derkins, Moe and Rosalyn. A lot of the content is also surprisingly still quite relatable in adulthood. How many times are we forced to do something we don’t want to do? How many times do we imagine we’re somewhere or someone else? Every morning before work, I’d try to get through 10-15 minutes worth of strips and every time I’d have to close the collection, I’d long for the next opportunity to escape back into Calvin’s world.<br /> </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11857278854502996982">The Indispensable Calvin and Hobbes By Bill Watterson is a hilarious book about a kid named Calvin and his pet (stuffed) tiger, Hobbes, and the book are many comics about Calvin’s life and extraordinary imagination. I especially love the longer comic, because they usually funnier. I love how Calvin and his parents don’t cooperate good, I can compare with my parents because I’m the brattiest child out of my siblings. If I had the time, I’d probably read all the other books. All I can find for the</span>
  <span id="freeText11857278854502996982" style="display:none">The Indispensable Calvin and Hobbes By Bill Watterson is a hilarious book about a kid named Calvin and his pet (stuffed) tiger, Hobbes, and the book are many comics about Calvin’s life and extraordinary imagination. I especially love the longer comic, because they usually funnier. I love how Calvin and his parents don’t cooperate good, I can compare with my parents because I’m the brattiest child out of my siblings. If I had the time, I’d probably read all the other books. All I can find for the author’s message is, let your imagination run wild, or do all the things you should do as a kid, besides go to school. I’d recommend this book to all children and people who love comedy.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2347046282" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4263609432778183738">I loved Calvin and Hobbes and I'm almost certain I own this, but it is in storage and I haven't seen it in over a decade. I was surprised at how some comics stuck with me almost word for word, while some seemed entirely new. It's also really neat how spending so much time with my niece has added a new dimension to these comic strips. I really love how nuanced Watterson's work is! <br/><br/>Perfect antidote to a miserable head cold. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15865486151167518784">I have not read many comics books in my reading career. In fact I think I have read none, so my opinion may not be valid. Even though the whole time Hobbes was just a stuffed animal, the author did an amazing job bringing the character of Hobbes to life. I definitely recommend this book as a comic if you have never read o</span>
  <span id="freeText15865486151167518784" style="display:none">I have not read many comics books in my reading career. In fact I think I have read none, so my opinion may not be valid. I had a great time reading The Indispensable Calvin and Hobbes. Throughout reading each story you developed a love for the relation of Calvin and Hobbes and wished it was real. Even though the whole time Hobbes was just a stuffed animal, the author did an amazing job bringing the character of Hobbes to life. I definitely recommend this book as a comic if you have never read one before, the changes in color and black and white makes the picture much for interesting. </span>

<div id="review_2986820629" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2986820629" />
    <a title="Victoria Miller" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1039390-victoria-miller"><img alt="Victoria Miller" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339622628p2/1039390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2986820629?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Victoria Miller" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Victoria Miller" href="/user/show/1039390-victoria-miller">Victoria Miller</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2986820629" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8147613081220040197">Actually, I've had this (and some others) for years, and usually at least once a year I grab one and go through it again. A wonderful way to read the comics with coffee and a croissant on a Sunday morning! And give yourself a lot of smiles, a few chortles, and even a few LOLs!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NnyuzzX3gWLZ5BP99gkZrOMU7SP3VX2Eh01x2P6R4+rTxiwONdNlXvwc6wUl4tK3yS+MeNLlf17CLbA+caLCMw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Yu707gVNU7HleMlvcpMfE5hZCfK011a6QlZmZj61mcOHVHYvBWm3jcCAMZeheNQIsmJoqZFnVGAHNqeAsYa4Gg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

It follows the humorous antics o<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText7684433328340464932\" style=\"display:none\">Please note that the content of this book primarily consists of articles available from Wikipedia or other free sources online. Calvin and Hobbes was a syndicated comic strip written and illustrated by Bill Watterson. It follows the humorous antics of Calvin, an imaginative six-year old boy, and Hobbes, his energetic and sardonic stuffed tiger. The pair are named after John Calvin, a 16th-century French Reformation theologian, and Thomas Hobbes, a 17th-century English political philosopher. The strip was syndicated daily from November 18, 1985 to December 31, 1995. At its height, Calvin and Hobbes was featured in over 2,400 newspapers worldwide. As of the publication of The Complete Calvin and Hobbes, more than 30 million copies of the 17 Calvin and Hobbes books had been sold. Set in the contemporary Midwestern United States in an unspecified suburban community, the broad themes of the strip deal with Calvin\'s flights of fantasy and his friendship with Hobbes, his misadventures, his unique views on a diverse range of political and cultural issues and his relationships with the people in his life, especially his parents. The dual nature of Hobbes is also a recurring motif: Calvin sees Hobbes as a live anthropomorphic tiger, while other characters see him as a stuffed toy.<\/span>\n  <a <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7811903803956839910">Bill Watterson (born William Boyd Watterson II) is an American cartoonist, and the author of the comic strip "Calvin and Hobbes". His career as a syndicated cartoonist ran from 1985 to 1995; he stopped drawing "Calvin and Hobbes" at the end of 1995 with a short statement to newspaper editors and his fans that he felt he had achieved all he could in the comic strip medium. During the early years of</span>
  <span id="freeText7811903803956839910" style="display:none">Bill Watterson (born William Boyd Watterson II) is an American cartoonist, and the author of the comic strip "Calvin and Hobbes". His career as a syndicated cartoonist ran from 1985 to 1995; he stopped drawing "Calvin and Hobbes" at the end of 1995 with a short statement to newspaper editors and his fans that he felt he had achieved all he could in the comic strip medium. During the early years of his career he produced several drawings and additional contributions for "Target: The Political Cartoon Quarterly". Watterson is known for his views on licensing and comic syndication, as well as for his reclusive nature.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7811903803956839910" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
